’ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред рдореВрд░реНрдзрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдиреГрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рд╕ рдЪрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕реЛ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рдЧреБрдгрдХреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдореБрджрд┐рддреЛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ-’ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реЗрдХреЛрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕реЛ рдореВрд░реНрдзрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕реМрд░реНрдпрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░реАрдпрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реНрдпреВрдврд╕реНрдп рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореЗрд╜рд╣рдиреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реБрдд рдПрддрджреНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░реАрдпрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ-’ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рдиреНрддрдордЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдЧреГрд╣рдкрддрд┐рдГ рд╕ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рео.рео) рдЗрддрд┐ редред

Jamison Brereton

88 (914)
Su╠Дrya and Vais╠Бva╠Дnara
M┼лrdhanvant ─Ас╣Еgirasa or V─Бmadevya
19 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Two simultaneous superimpositions structure this hymn. On the one hand, the present-day sacrifice involving the establishment of the ritual fire and the pouring of oblations into it is contrasted with the primal production of the sacrificial fire by the gods. The present-day sacrifice begins (vs. 1ab) and ends (vs. 19) the hymn, and periodically surfaces throughout (vss. 3, 5, 14). However, the dominant strain is the primordial one, which begins in the second half of verse 1; the role of the gods in creating the original sacrifice and тАЬbegettingтАЭ the sacrificial fire is especially emphasized in verses 4 and the long sequence of 7тАУ13, where the phrase тАЬthe gods begotтАЭ appears four times (vss. 8тАУ10, 13), alongside similar expressions. This the matic strain is especially striking because the gods are also regularly identified as тАЬworthy of the sacrificeтАЭ (vss. 3, 6, 11, 13; see also 5, where Agni is so called), that is, worthy of receiving the sacrifice, while they are in fact performing the sacrifice.
The other theme of superimposition is the identification of Agni, especially under the epithet Vai┼Ыv─Бnara тАЬbelonging to all men,тАЭ with the sun. At first the sunтАЩs dependence on and complementarity with Agni is mentioned (vss. 1b, 2, 6): the sun only becomes visible and begins to shine when Agni is also visible. But the cosmos-filling radiance and heat of Agni (see vss. 3, 5, 7, 9) leads gradually to the premise that the gods created Agni as the sun, expressed clearly in verses 10тАУ13. The poet then acknowledges Agni as the sun (vs. 14) and in enigmatic language describes the two paths between heaven and earth along which the sun / cosmic fire moves (vss. 15тАУ16).
The last three verses (17тАУ19) seem to provide a simultaneous transition from the cosmic and primordial elements in the superimposed structures to the present-day everydayтАФby way of a dialogue between two unnamed participants. Most interpreters (e.g., Geldner and Renou) identify the speakers as two priests, probably the Brahman and Hotar who are explicitly mentioned in the last p─Бda of the last verse (19d). But the words that introduce the speakers in verse 17, a╠Бvara and pa╠Бra, are ambiguous. They can mean тАЬnearerтАЭ and тАЬfartherтАЭ (referring to the positions of the priests on the sacrificial ground), but they can also mean тАЬlowerтАЭ and тАЬupperтАЭ / тАЬbelowтАЭ and тАЬabove,тАЭ as derivatives of these words do in verse 14. In verse 17 they can therefore refer to cosmic elements. It is our view that in verse 17 the dialogue is first presented as a debate between Earth and Heaven (which appear at the end of vs. 15 as the defining poles of the cosmos) about their roles in sacrifice, but the dialogue participants unobtrusively become transformed into present-day priests.
The final verse anchors us firmly in the here-and-now of the sacrifice, but also asserts that as long as the morning fire will be kindled and the dawns will dawn, the sacrifice as we know it will be performed. This assertion may involve a bit of propa ganda. The term br─Бhmaс╣З├б as the technical designation of a priest appears in this verse; this term was only introduced in the late R╠еgveda (as opposed to the earlier brahma╠Бn тАЬformulatorтАЭ), presumably as part of a codification and partial reorgani zation of the sacrificial system. The poet may then be claiming a long future for the new system, and implicitly suggesting its long history, stretching back to the origins of the worldтАФcloaking a religious innovation in a garment of imagined tradition, as so often.

рдкрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдкрд╛рдиреАрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рддреНрдордХрдореН рдЕрдЬрд░рдВ рдЬрд░рд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдпрддреН рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджрд┐ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд░рд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдкреГрд╢рд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рд╕реНрдкреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд░рд┐ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМ рдЖрд╣реБрддрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╣реБрддрдВ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реЛрдорд╛рддреНрдордХрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ рднрд░реНрдордгреЗ рднрд░рдгрд╛рдп рднреБрд╡рдирд╛рдп рднрд╛рд╡рдирд╛рдп рдЪ рдзрд░реНрдордгреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдп рдЪ рдХрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдорд┐рдордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрдпрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрди рдкрдкреНрд░рдердиреНрдд рдкреНрд░рдердпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ-тАЩ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрдпрддреНрдкрд╛рдиреАрдпрдордЬрд░рдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рджрд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрдкреГрд╢реНрдпрднрд┐рд╣реБрддрдВ рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрдордЧреНрдиреМ рддрд╕реНрдп рднрд░рдгрд╛рдп рдЪ рднрд╛рд╡рдирд╛рдп рдЪ рдзрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдп рдЪреИрддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднреНрдпреЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЗрдордордЧреНрдирд┐рдордиреНрдиреЗрдирд╛рдкрдкреНрд░рдердиреНрдд’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рен, реирел) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma oblation, undecaying and agreeable to the gods, which is offered to Agni, who is cognizantof heaven, who touches the sky– for its nourishment, existence and support, the gods supply (Agni) the giver ofhappiness with food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Gods supply: Nirukta 8.25

Jamison Brereton

The oblation, the drink, unaging and delightful, has been poured into Agni, the one who finds the sun and touches heaven.
For him to bear and support the world, the gods spread out (the world) by their autonomous power.

Griffith

DEAR, ageless sacrificial drink is offered in light-discovering, heaven-pervading Agni.
The Gods spread forth through his Celestial Nature, that he might bear the world up and sustain it.

Geldner

Das Trankopfer, das nicht alternde, ist in dem sonnenfindenden, zum Himmel reichenden Agni geopfert, das genehme. Durch seine Eigenkraft breiteten sich die G├╢tter aus, um die Welt zu tragen, zu erhalten.

Grassmann

Ergossen ist der Opfertrank, der ew’ge, dem Agni lieb, dem lichten Himmelsst├╝rmer, Ihn breiteten mit Sch├╢pferkraft die G├╢tter der Welt zur St├╝tze aus, um sie zu tragen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe whole world swallowed up, hidden in darkness, was made manifest when Agni was born; thegods, heaven and earth, the waters and the plural nts rejoiced in his friendship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The world was swallowed and hidden away by darkness; (then) the sun became manifest when Agni was born.
The gods, Earth and Heaven, and the waters and plants took pleasure in the fellowship of this one, of him.

Griffith

The world was swallowed and concealed in darkness: Agni was born, and light became apparent.
The Deities, the broad earth, and the heavens, and plants, and waters gloried in his friendship.

Geldner

Verschlungen war die Welt, von Finsternis verh├╝llt, die Sonne kam zum Vorschein, als Agni geboren wurde. In seiner Freundschaft wurden die G├╢tter, Erde, Himmel und die Gew├дsser, die Pflanzen froh.

Grassmann

Verschlungen war die Welt, verh├╝llt vom Dunkel; Lichtglanz erschien, als Agni ward geboren; An seiner Freundschaft labten sich die G├╢tter, die Erd’, der Himmel, Wasser und Gew├дchse.

Elizarenkova

тАЬSent by adorable gods I praise the undecaying and mighty Agni, who by his radiance has spread forththe earth and this heaven, the two worlds and the firmament.тАЭ

Now urged on by the gods worthy of the sacrifice, I shall praise Agni, unaging and lofty,
who with his radiance stretches through earth and this heaven, through the two world-halves and the midspace.

Inspired by Gods who claim our adoration, I now will laud Eternal Lofty Agni,
Him who hath spread abroad the earth with lustre, this heaven, and both the worlds, and air’s mid-region.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho propitiated by the gods was the first offerer of oblations, whom his worshippers anoint withclarified butter– he, Agni J─Бtavedas, quickly made that which can fly, that which can walk, that which isstationary, that which is moveable.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nirukta 5.3

Jamison Brereton

He who was the first Hotar, delightful to the gods, whom they anointed with melted butter upon choosing him (as priest),
he made what flies and what goes (on foot), the still and the moving, to wax strongтАФAgni J─Бtavedas.

Griffith

Earliest Priest whom all the Gods accepted, and chose him, and anointed him with butter,
He swiftly made all things that fly, stand, travel, all that hath motion, Agni Jatavedas.

Geldner

Der der erste gottgenehme Hotri war, den sie erw├дhlend mit Schmalz salbten. Er hat das Fliegende und das Gehende, was steht und lebt, gedeihlich gemacht, der Agni Jatavedas.

Grassmann

Der erste Priester er, der Gott-erw├╝nschte, den liebend man mit Opferschmalz besalbte, Was fliegt, was geht, was steht, was sich beweget, macht’ dienstbar sich der Wesenkenner Agni.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрдГ рдЬрд╛рддрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдпрддреН рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рднреБрд╡рдирд╕реНрдп рддреНрд░реИрд▓реЛрдХреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдореВрд░реНрдзрдиреН рдореВрд░реНрдзрдирд┐ рд░реЛрдЪрдиреЗрди рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рдЕрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардГ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ рддрдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдорддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреАрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЧреАрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реИрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрд╣реЗрдо рдкреНрд░рдкрджреНрдпрд╛рдорд╣реЗ ред ’ рд╣рд┐ рдЧрддреМ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдзрд╛рддреБрдГ ред рд╕рдГ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд░реЛрджрд╕рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдГ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрдГ рдкреВрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╢реНрд╡ рдЕрднрд╡рдГ рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рее рее резреж рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as you abide, Agni J─Бtavedas, on the brow of the universe, together with the sun, we havecome to you with praises, with hymns, with prayers; you are adorable, the satisfier of heaven and earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When, o Agni J─Бtavedas, you stood at the head of the world together with your light,
we spurred you on with thoughts, songs, and recitations. You became worthy of the sacrifice as the one filling the two world-halves.

Griffith

Because thou, Agni, Jatavedas, stoodest at the world’s head with thy refulgent splendour,
We sent thee forth with hymns and songs and praises: thou filledst heaven and earth, God meet for worship.

Geldner

Da du, Jatavedas, an die Spitze der Welt tratest, mit deinem Lichtglanz, o Agni, da haben wir dich mit Gedichten, mit Lobliedern, mit Preisreden angespornt. Du wurdest opferw├╝rdig, die Welt erf├╝llend.

Grassmann

Als an des Himmels Haupt du standest, Agni, o Wesenkenner, mit dem Glanz der Welten, Da priesen wir mit Liedern dich und Spr├╝chen, da warst du opferwerth, die Welt erf├╝llend.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni is the head of all beings by night; then the sun rising early is born; (the wise know) this to be thewisdom of the adorable gods, that the swift- moving sun being intelligent moves through the firmameс╣Зс╣нтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Firmament: Nirukta 7.27;

Apas = karma, function;

M─Бy─Б: illusion

Jamison Brereton

Agni becomes the head of the world by night; thence is the sun born, rising early in the morning.
(Behold) this artful contrivance of those worthy of the sacrifice, that the swift one pursues his work, knowing the way.

Griffith

Head of the world is Agni in the night-time; then, as the Sun, at morn springs up and rises.
Then to his task goes the prompt Priest foreknowing the wondrous power of Gods who must be honoured.

Geldner

Des Nachts ist Agni das Haupt der Erde; aus ihm wird am Morgen der aufgehende Surya geboren. Seht doch dieses Kunstst├╝ck der opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter, da├Я er p├╝nktlich an sein Werk geht, des Weges kundig;

Grassmann

Der Erde Haupt ist Agni in den N├дchten, dann steigt er fr├╝h als Sonne auf am Morgen; Wenn eilend er ans Werk geht, wohl erkennend die Zaubermacht der altehrw├╝rd’gen G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Lovely is he who, kindled in his greatness, hath shone forth, seated in the heavens, refulgent.
With resonant hymns all Gods who guard our bodies have offered up oblation in this Agni.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods first genitive rated the words of the hymn, then Agni, then the oblation; he is the (object of the)sacrifice of these deities, the protector of the body; him the heaven knows, him the earth and the waters, know.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The gods first begot well-spoken speech, after that the fire [/Agni], after that the oblation.
This became their sacrifice, the protector of bodies. That does Heaven know, that does Earth, that the waters.

Griffith

First the Gods brought the hymnal into being; then they engendered Agni, then oblation.
He was their satrifice that guards our bodies: him the heavens know, the earth, the waters know him.

Geldner

Die G├╢tter erschufen zuerst den Liedvortrag, dann den Agni, dann die Opferspende. Dies ward ihr Opfer, das sie selbst sch├╝tzt. Dieses kennt der Himmel, dieses die Erde, dieses das Wasser.

Grassmann

Den sch├╢nen Sang zuerst, darauf den Agni, den Opferguss dann schufen sich die G├╢tter; Er ward ihr Opfer, das den Leib besch├╝tzet, ihn kennt die Erd’, ihn Himmel und Gew├дsser.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni whom the gods genitive rated, in whom all beings have offered oblations– he, the straight-going, haswarmed by his \radiance, by his might, the earth and his heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The fire [/Agni] whom the gods begot, in whom all beings poured oblations,
aiming straight, he heated earth and this heaven with his flame in his greatness.

Griffith

He, Agni, whom the Gods have generated, in whom they offered up all worlds and creatures,
He with his bright glow heated earth and heaven, urging himself right onward in his grandeur.

Geldner

Agni, den die G├╢tter erschufen, in dem sie alle Welten opferten, der erhitzte mit seinem Strahl die Erde und diesen Himmel mit Macht in redlicher Absicht.

Grassmann

Er, Agni, den die G├╢tterschar erzeugte, in welchen alle Wesen Opfer giessen, Er w├дrmte Erd’ und Himmel hier mit Strahlen, mit seiner Gr├╢sse grad’ empor sich richtend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods have by praise engendered Agni in the sky, who fills heaven and earth by his functions, theyappointed the joy-bestowing Agni to his three- fold condition, he brings the manifold plural nts to maturity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three-foldcondition: i.e., either to his plural ce at the three daily sacrifices, or his position in heaven the firmament, and earth,as the sun, lightning, and fire. Nirukta 7.28 cites a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, that Agni, in his third capacity in heaven, is thesun

Jamison Brereton

For with a praise song, with their powers the gods begot in heaven the fire [/Agni] that fills the world-halves.
And, for the sake of the world, they made him threefold. He ripens the plants of all forms.

Griffith

Then by the laud the Gods engendered Agni in heaven, who fills both worlds through strength and vigour.
They made him to appear in threefold essence: he ripens plants of every form and nature.

Denn unter Preislied hatten die G├╢tter im Himmel den Agni erzeugt, der mit seinen Kr├дften die Welt erf├╝llt. Sie machten, da├Я er sich dreifach teilte. Er bringt die verschiedenartigen Pflanzen zur Reife.

Grassmann

Denn G├╢tter zeugten durch Gesang am Himmel den Agni, dass mit Kraft die Welt er f├╝llte, Ihn schufen sie, dass dreifach er erscheine; die allgestalt’gen Pflanzen l├дsst er reifen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen the adorable gods, plural ced him and S┼лrya, the son of Aditi, in heaven; when the swift-movingpair (Agni and Vai┼Ыv─Бnara) appeared, then all beings beheld them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Swift-moving pair: the dawn and the suс╣ЕNirukta 7.29

Jamison Brereton

When the gods worthy of the sacrifice set him in heaven as the Sun, the son of Aditi,
when the wandering pair [=Sun and Moon?] came into existence, only after that did all living beings see in front of (them).

Griffith

What time the Gods, whose due is worship, set him as Surya, Son of Aditi, in heaven,
When the Pair, ever wandering, sprang to being, all creatures that existed looked upon them.

Geldner

Als die opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter ihn an den Himmel setzten, den Surya, der Aditi Sohn, als das wandelnde Paar erschien, da erst sahen alle Welten.

Grassmann

Als an den Himmel ihn die heil’gen setzten, als Sonnengott die G├╢tter den Aditja, Als beide Zwillingswanderer erstanden, da konnten vor sich schauen alle Wesen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe gods made Agni Vai┼Ыv─Бnara, the indicator of days, for the sake of the whole world, whostretched out the radiant dawns, and as he moves along scatters the darkness with his light.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the sake of the whole world the gods made Agni Vai┼Ыv─Бnara the beacon of the days.
He who extends through the radiant dawns uncovers the darkness as he goes with his flame.

Griffith

For all the world of life the Gods made Agni Vaisvanara to be the days’ bright Banner,-
Him who hath spread abroad the radiant Mornings, and, coming with his light, unveils the darkness.

Geldner

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWe glorify daily with praises the brilliant and sage Agni Vai┼Ыv─Бnara, the god who overcomes by hismight both heaven and earth, (burning) both below and above.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With mantras we address the poet Agni Vai┼Ыv─Бnara shining everywhere, the god who by his greatness encompasses the two wide (worlds) from below and from above.

Griffith

We call upon the Sage with holy verses, Agni Vaisvanara the ever-beaming,
Who hath surpassed both heaven and earth in greatness: lie is a God below, a God above us.

Geldner

Den Vaisvanara, den allezeit leuchtenden, den Agni, den Seher, rufen wir mit Dichterworten an, den Gott, der mit seiner Gr├╢├Яe die beiden breiten Welth├дlften umspannt, sowohl von unten als von oben.

Grassmann

Den M├дnnerhort, der Tag f├╝r Tag erstrahlet, den weisen Agni preisen wir mit Spr├╝chen Der beide Welten ├╝berragt an Gr├╢sse, der Gott im untern und im obern Raume.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI have heard that there are two paths for Pitс╣Ыs, gods and mortals; all this universe which is betweenthe paternal (heaven) and the maternal (earth) proceeds on its way by these two (paths).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 19.27; the twopaths, the pitс╣Ыy─Бna and the devay─Бna are describedin Bhagavadg─лt─Б 7.24 o 26

Jamison Brereton

I have heard from the forefathers that there are two routes, (that of) the gods and (that of) mortals.
Along those two everything that moves goes together, whatever is between the father [=Heaven] and the mother [=Earth].

Griffith

I have heard mention of two several pathways, ways of the Fathers and of Gods and mortals.
On these two paths each moving creature travels, each thing between the Father and the Mother.

Geldner

Zwei Wege, so h├╢rte ich von den V├дtern, gibt es f├╝r die G├╢tter und die Sterblichen. Auf diesen beiden kommt all dies Lebendige zusammen, das zwischen dem Vater, dem Himmel, und der Mutter, der Erde, ist.

Grassmann

Zwei Pfade gibt’s, so sagten mir die V├дter, den G├╢ttern gangbar und den Menschenkindern, Auf ihnen wandelt alles, was sich reget, was zwischen Erd’ und Himmel ist, den Aeltern.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe associated two (heaven and earth) support (Agni) moving, born from the head, sanctified bypraise; diligent, rapid, radiant, he appears in the presence of all beings.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Born from the head: or born from─Аditya, the head, or chief, of all things

Jamison Brereton

Conjoined, the two carry the one that wanders, born from the head, stroked by mind.
He stands facing all beings: not keeping his distance, as, gleaming, he makes his transit.

Griffith

These two united paths bear him who journeys born from the head and pondered with the spirit
He stands directed to all things existing, hasting, unresting in his fiery splendour.

Geldner

Die beiden gepaarten, Himmel und Erde, tragen den Wandelnden, den aus ihrem Haupte Geborenen, den im Geiste Betrachteten. Er steht da, allen Welten zugewandt, nie nachl├дssig, durchhaltend, strahlend.

Grassmann

Vereinigt tragen beide sie den Wandrer, den Haupt-entstammten, mit Verstand geschm├╝ckten; Auf alle Wesen blickend steht er strahlend, das All durchdringend, nimmer ferne weilend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the lower and upper (fire) disputed “which of us twain leaders of sacrifice knows the work best?“then the friends (the priests) were competent (to offer) sacrifice, they came to the sacrifice; who declares this?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lower and upper fire: the lower fire is Agni, or the terrestrial fire; the upper fire is V─Бyu, or the intermediate fire

Jamison Brereton

When the lower [/nearer] one and the higher [/farther] one debate with each other, (they ask) тАЬOf the two leaders of the sacrifice, which of us two knows it through and through?тАЭ
Have our comrades been able to achieve joint revelry? Have they realized the sacrifice? Who can proclaim this here?

Griffith

Which of us twain knows where they speak together, upper and lower of the two rite-leaders?
Our friends have helped to gather our assembly. They came to sacrifice; who will announce it?

Geldner

├Ьber den beide einen Wortstreit f├╝hren, h├╝ben und dr├╝ben sitzend: Welcher von uns beiden Opferleitern wei├Я es genau? Die Genossen haben die gemeinsame Trankfeier zustande gebracht, sie kamen zum Opfer. Wer wird Folgendes beantworten?

Grassmann

Wo sich der untre und der obre sprechen, wer weiss das von uns Opferleitern beiden, Des Festes Mahl bereiteten die Freunde, zum Opfer kamen sie, wer wird es kund thun?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHow many fires are there, how many suns, how many dawns, how many waters? I address you, OPitс╣Ыs, not in rivalry, I ask you, sages, in order to know (the truth).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАЬHow many fires are there and how many suns? How many dawns, and how many waters?
O forefathers, I am not saying something two-faced to you: o poets, I am asking you in order to know.тАЭ

Griffith

How many are the Fires and Suns in number? What is the number of the Dawns and Waters?
Not jestingly I speak to you, O Fathers. Sages, I ask you this for information.

Geldner

Wie viele Feuer gibt es, wie viele Sonnen, wie viele Morgenr├╢ten, wie viele sind denn die Gew├дsser? Ich stelle euch keine verf├дngliche Frage, ihr V├дter; ich frage euch, ihr Seher, nur um es zu erfahren.”

Grassmann

рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрдирд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рд░реНрдгрдпрдордирдпрд╛ рд╡рджрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рддрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рдорд╛рддрд░реНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдиреН рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ рдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рджреЗрд╡ рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдкрддрдирд╛ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдВ рдореБрдЦрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ ред рди рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рд╡рд╕рддреЗ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╡рдд рдПрд╡ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдГ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдЕрд╡рд░рдГ рдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдГ рд╣реЛрддреБрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рд╕реНрдп рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╣реЛрддреБрдГ рдирд┐рд╖реАрджрдиреН рд╣реМрддреНрд░рдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░реНрддреБрдореБрдкрд╡рд┐рд╢рдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд╛рдпрди рдЙрдкрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдЙрдк рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ ред рд╣реЛрддреГрдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реНрд╡рдмреБрджреНрдзреМ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ-тАЩ рдпрд╛рд╡рдиреНрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдореБрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд░реНрд╢рдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрдпреБрдкрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧ рдЗрд╣реЗрд╡ рдирд┐рдзреЗрд╣реАрддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдкрддрдирд╛ рдПрддрд╛ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпреЛ рд╡рд╕рддреЗ рдорд╛рддрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдЮреНрдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╕реНрдп рддрд╛рд╡рджреБрдкрджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрд╣реЛрддреБрд░рд╡рд░реЛ рдирд┐рд╖реАрджрдиреН рд╣реЛрддреГрдЬрдкрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдирдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░реАрдпреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. рен. рейрез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рее рее резрей рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs long, M─Бtari┼Ыvan, as the swiftly-moving (nights) cover the face of the dawn, (so long) theBrahman, the inferior sitting down (to perform the work) of the Hot─Б, approaching the sacrifice supports (theceremony).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For as long as the fine-feathered (mares [=flames?]) clothe themselves as if in the face of Dawn, o M─Бtari┼Ыvan,
for that long the Brahmin establishes (the fire), approaching the
sacrifice and taking his seat near to the Hotar.

Griffith

As great as is the fair-winged Morning’s presence to him who dwells beside us, matarisvan!
Is what the Brahman does when he approaches to sacrifice and sits below the Hotar.

Geldner

Noch ehe die befl├╝gelten Flammen sich mit dem Abglanz der Morgenr├╢ten umkleiden, o Matarisvan, stellt bei dem Opfer erscheinend der Brahmane auf die Probe, dem Hotri gegen├╝ber Platz nehmend.

Grassmann

So lang die sch├╢nbeschwingten, Matari├зvan! sich kleiden in der Morgenr├╢the Strahlen, So lange wirkt beim Opfer der Brahmane sich niederlassend zu des Priesters F├╝ssen.

Elizarenkova

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛рддрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдиреН)рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ ! рд╣реЗ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЙрд╖рд╛рд╡реЗрд▓рд╛ рддрдм рддрдХ рдХрд╣рд▓рд╛рддреА рд╣реИ, рдЬрдм рддрдХ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ рдЙрд╕реЗ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрд┐рдд рди рдХрд░ рджреЗрдВ, рдЬрдм рдврдХ рджреЗрдВ, рддрдм рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЖрд░рдореНрдн рдХрд░реЗ, рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рдирд╣реАрдВ, рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рддреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреА рд╡реЗрд▓рд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрепрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛рддрд░рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреН) рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ ! рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдореН) рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрдореН-рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдВ рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ (рди) рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рддрд┐ тАЬрдЙрдкрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдГтАЭ [рдирд┐рд░реБреж ренредрейрез] (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгреНрдпрдГ-рд╡рд╕рддреЗ) рд╕реБрдкрддрдирд╛рдГ рдкрддрддреНрд░рдпреЛ рд╡рд╕рддреЗ-рдЙрд╖рд╕рдВ рдЫрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рддрд╛рд╡рддреН) рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╣реЛрддреБрдГ) рд╣реЛрддреГрднреВрддрд╕реНрдп-рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ (рдЕрд╡рд░рдГ-рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдГ) рдЕрд╡рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ (рдирд┐рд╖реАрджрдиреН) рдЙрдкрд╡рд┐рд╢рдиреН (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН-рдЖрдпрдиреН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН (рддрд╛рд╡рддреН-рдЙрдкрджрдзрд╛рддрд┐) рддрд╛рд╡рддреНрдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рддрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореБрдк рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ реерезрепрее
